25:T9a8d,<entryFree id="n28681" key="عَرُضَ" type="main">

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَرُضَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">عَرُضَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عِرَضٌ</foreign>, [instead of which, as a simple subst., <foreign lang="ar">عَرْضٌ</foreign> is generally used,] and <foreign lang="ar">عَرَاضَةٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, broad,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">wide;</hi> (S, O, * Msb, K, TA;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-1" target="اعرض" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28683"/></foreign>, (A, TA,) which occurs in this sense in two exs. following. (TA.) [And in like manner,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-2" target="استعرض" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28687"/></foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It grew,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">spread, wide;</hi> said of a tree; opposed to <foreign lang="ar">طَالَ</foreign>; occurring in the TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">بهل</foreign>.] It is said in a prov., <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-3" target="أَعْرَضَتِ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>القِرْفَةُ</foreign> (S, O, * TA [but in two copies of the S, I find the verb in this instance written <foreign lang="ar">اعرضتُ</foreign>, and in the O <foreign lang="ar">اعرضتَ</foreign>, and I do not know that the reading in the TA, which seems to be the common one, is found in any copy of the S,]) <hi rend="ital">Suspicion became,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has become, wide;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِتَّسَعَت</foreign>: (TA:) used when it is said to a man, “ Whom dost thou suspect ? ” and he answers, “ The sons of such a one, ” referring to the whole tribe. (S, O, TA.) [See Freytag's Arab. Prov. ii. 112, where another reading is mentioned, which, by what he says, is shown to be <foreign lang="ar">أَعْرَضْتَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">القِرْفَةَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Thou hast made suspicion wide.</hi>] In another prov. it is said, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-4" target="أَعْرَضَ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ثَوْبُ المَلْبَسِ</foreign> (IAar, A, TA, and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">لبس</foreign>,) and <foreign lang="ar">المِلْبَسِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">المُلْبِسِ</foreign> (IAar, and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">لبس</foreign>,) and <foreign lang="ar">المُلْتَبِسِ</foreign> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">لبس</foreign>) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">صَارَ ذَا عَرْضٍ</foreign>, (A, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">عَرُضَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">اِتَّسَعَ</foreign>; (Sh;) [meaning the same as the prov. before mentioned;] used with reference to him whose suspicion has become wide; (IAar, and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">لبس</foreign>;) i. e. with reference to him who suspects many persons (IAar, Az, and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">لبس</foreign>,) of a theft; (IAar, Az, and TA in that art.;) or of saying a thing: (TS, and TA in that art.:) or when thou askest a person respecting a thing and he does not explain it to thee. (TA in that art.) [See, again, Freytag's Arab. Prov. ii. 100, where it is said that <foreign lang="ar">أَعْرَضَ ثَوْبُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المُلْبِسِ</foreign> app. means <hi rend="ital">The garment of the suspected appeared,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has appeared:</hi> but that another reading is <foreign lang="ar">عَرُضَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">became,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has become, wide.</hi>]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَضَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَرِضَ</orth>
                  </form>, (Fr, S, O, Msb, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَرْضٌ</foreign>; (TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">عَرِضَ</foreign>, (As, TS, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">عَرَضَ</orth>
                  </form>, (Fr, K,) or      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَرِضَ</orth>
                  </form>, like <foreign lang="ar">حَسِبَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَرِضَ</orth>
                  </form>, deviating from the general rule; (As, TS;) <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a thing) <hi rend="ital">appeared,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became apparent,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">to him;</hi> (S, O, Msb, K; [but in some copies of the K, instead of the explanation <foreign lang="ar">ظَهَرَ وَبَدَا</foreign>, we find <foreign lang="ar">ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهِ وَبَدَا</foreign>, which is a mistake;]) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-5" target="اعرض" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28683"/></foreign>, (Fr, S, O, Msb, K,) which is a deviation from a general rule, being quasi pass. of <foreign lang="ar">عَرَضَهُ</foreign>, which see below; (S, * O, * Msb, K;) [lit.] <hi rend="ital">it showed its breadth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">width.</hi> (O, * TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-6" target="اعرض" n="6" type="8" subtype="FSOTF" lang="ar" select="n28683"/>لَكَ الشَّىْءُ مِنْ بَعِيدٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The thing appeared to thee from afar.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">عَرَضَتْ لَهُ الغُولُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَرِضَتْ</foreign>, (AZ, S, O, K,) <hi rend="ital">The ghool appeared to him.</hi> (K.) The Arabs say, of a thing, <foreign lang="ar">عَرَضَ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-7" target="اعرض" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28683"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-8" target="تعرّض" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28684"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-9" target="اعترض" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28686"/></foreign>, using these verbs as syn.; (Sh;) [app. as meaning <hi rend="ital">It showed, presented,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">offered, itself,</hi> (lit. <hi rend="ital">its breadth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">width,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">its side,</hi> see 5,) to a person: the first and last also often signify, and the others sometimes, <hi rend="ital">he obtruded himself</hi> in an affair; <hi rend="ital">interfered</hi> therein:] IKt disallows   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-10" target="اعرض" n="10" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28683"/></foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">اعترض</foreign>, as not having been found by him: (TA:) [but] an instance of the former of these two verbs used in the sense of the latter of them occurs in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا <ref cref="n28681-11" target="أُعْرَضَتْ" n="11" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لِلنَّاظِرِينَ</foreign> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">When she shows,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">presents, herself to the lookers</hi>], in a poem by one of the tribe of Teiyi. (Sh.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَضَ لَكَ الخَيْرُ</foreign>, [in one place in the TA <foreign lang="ar">الخَبَرَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">الخبر</foreign> in a copy of the Msb,] inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَرْضٌ</foreign>; (TA; [in one place in the TA <foreign lang="ar">عُرُوضٌ</foreign> there referring to <foreign lang="ar">الخَبَرُ</foreign>, which is app. a mistranscription;]) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-12" target="اعرض" n="12" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28683"/></foreign>; (S, O, K, TA;) <hi rend="ital">Good</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">the doing of good</hi>] <hi rend="ital">hath become within thy power,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">practicable to thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">easy to thee.</hi> (S, O, K, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28681-13" target="اعرض" n="13" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n28683"/>لَكَ الظَّبْىُ</foreign>

(TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  See also 1, near the end, in three places.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تَعَرِيضٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">The speaking obliquely, indirectly, obscurely, ambiguously,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">equivocally; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَصْرِيحٌ</foreign>; (S, Mgh, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">as when thou askest a man,</hi> “ <hi rend="ital">Hast thou seen such a one?</hi> ” <hi rend="ital">and he, having seen him, and disliking to lie, answers,</hi> “ <hi rend="ital">Verily such a one is seen:</hi> ” (Msb:) or the <hi rend="ital">making a phrase,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, to convey an allusion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an indication not expressly mentioned therein; as when you say</hi> “ <hi rend="ital">How foul is niggardliness!</hi> ” <hi rend="ital">alluding to such a one's being a niggard</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">تُعَرِّضُ بِأَنَّهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَخِيلٌ</foreign>): differing from <foreign lang="ar">كِنَايَةٌ</foreign>, which is the mentioning of the consequence and meaning that of which it is the consequence; as when you say “ Such a one has a long suspensory cord to his sword, and has many ashes of the cooking-pot; ” meaning that he is tall of stature, and one who entertains many guests: (Mgh:) [but many hold these two words to be identical in meaning.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">عَرَّضْتُ لِفُلَانٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِفُلَانٍ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">I said something</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in the manner explained above</hi>], <hi rend="ital">meaning such a one.</hi> (S, Msb.) [See also an ex. voce <foreign lang="ar">كَلَّآءٌ</foreign>.] 'Omar defined [or rather explained] <foreign lang="ar">التَّعْرِيضُ بِالفَاحِشَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The making an allusion to that which is foul,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">obscene</hi>] by the instance of a man saying to another “ My father is not an adulterer, nor is my mother an adulteress. ” (O, TA.) Or, accord. to the early authorities, <foreign lang="ar">عرّض</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">He used a phrase susceptible of different meanings,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an equivocal phrase, by which the hearer understood a meaning different from that which he</hi> (<hi rend="ital">the speaker</hi>) <hi rend="ital">intended:</hi> or, accord. to the later authorities, as Et-Teftezánee, <hi rend="ital">he mentioned a thing by a proper or tropical or metonymical expression, to signify some other thing, which he did not mention;</hi> as when one says, “ I heard him whom thou hatest praying for thee, and making good mention of thee; ” meaning in his praying for the Muslims in general. (El-Munáwee, in explaining the trad. <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ فِى المَعَارِيضِ الخ</foreign>, which see below, voce <foreign lang="ar">مِعْرَاضٌ</foreign>.) <foreign lang="ar">تعريض</foreign> with respect to the demanding of a woman in marriage in [the period of] her <foreign lang="ar">عِدَّة</foreign>, [during which she may not contract a new marriage,] is the using language which resembles a demand of her in marriage, but does not plainly express it; as the saying to her “ Verily thou art beautiful, ” or “ Verily there is a desire for thee, ” or “ Verily women are of the things that I need: ” and <foreign lang="ar">تعريض</foreign> is sometimes made by the quoting of proverbs, and by the introducing of enigmas in one's speech. (TA.)                      <L>

                  </quote> in which <foreign lang="ar">عِرْض</foreign> cannot be syn. with <foreign lang="ar">بَدَن</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">جِسْم</foreign>, for, were it so, it would involve a contradiction; the meaning being only <hi rend="ital">Many a person meagre</hi> in respect of his body <hi rend="ital">is noble</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">great</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in respect of his ancestry;</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and fat in respect of the body, meagre in respect of grounds of pretension to honour on account of the honourable deeds or qualities of his ancestors,</hi> &amp;c.:] and by Mohammad's using the expression <foreign lang="ar">دَمُهُ وَعِرْضُهُ</foreign>; for if <foreign lang="ar">عِرْض</foreign> were [here] syn. with <foreign lang="ar">نَفْس</foreign>, it had sufficed to say <foreign lang="ar">دمه</foreign> without <foreign lang="ar">عرضه</foreign>.                      <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عُرْضَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فُعْلَةٌ</foreign> in the sense of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مَفْعولٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">قُبْضَةٌ</foreign>; (Bd, ii. 224;) and is applied to <hi rend="ital">A thing that is set as an obstacle in the way of a thing:</hi> (Bd, TA:) and also to <hi rend="ital">a thing that is exposed to a thing:</hi> (Bd:) or <hi rend="ital">that is set as a butt, like the butt of archers.</hi> (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">جَعَلْتُ فُلَانًا عُرْضَةً لِكَذَا</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">نَصَبْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَهُ</foreign>; (S, O, K; *) i. e. <hi rend="ital">I set such a one as an obstacle to such a thing:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">as a butt for such a thing.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ لَهُ دُونَهُ عُرْضَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He is an obstacle to him intervening in the way of it.</hi> (S, O.) And <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ عُرْضَةٌ لِلنَّاسِ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">They are weak persons; persons who offer themselves as a prey to any one who would take them.</hi> (TA.) And it is said in the Kur [ii. 224], <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا تَجْعَلُوا</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّاسِ</foreign>, (S, * &amp;c.,) meaning <foreign lang="ar">نَصْبًا</foreign>; (S, TA;) admitting the two significations of <hi rend="ital">an obstacle</hi> and <hi rend="ital">a butt:</hi> (TA:) i. e. <hi rend="ital">And make not God an obstacle</hi> between you and that which may bring you near unto God, &amp;c.: (O, K:) or <hi rend="ital">make not God an obstacle to the performance of your oaths to be pious</hi> (O, Bd) <hi rend="ital">and to fear God and to make reconciliation between men:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">make not God an obstacle, because of your oaths, to your being pious</hi> &amp;c.: (Bd:) or <hi rend="ital">make not the swearing by God an obstacle to your being pious</hi> [&amp;c.]: (Fr:) and Zj says the like of this: (L:) or <foreign lang="ar">عُرْضَةٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">intervention</hi> with respect to good and evil; (Abu-l- 'Abbás, O, K;) and the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">do not intervene by swearing by God every little while so as not to be pious</hi> &amp;c.: (O, K, * TA:) or <hi rend="ital">make not God an object of your oaths, by ordinary and frequent swearing by Him,</hi> (Bd,) or <hi rend="ital">a butt for your oaths, like the butt of archers,</hi> (TA,) <hi rend="ital">in order that ye may be pious</hi> &amp;c.; for the habitual swearer emboldens himself against God, and is not pious &amp;c.: (Bd:) or, as some say, the meaning is <hi rend="ital">make not the mention of God a means of strengthening your oaths.</hi> (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا عُرْضَةٌ لَكَ</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">This is a thing prepared for thy common,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ordinary, use.</hi> (O, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A purpose; an intention;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an object of desire,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of endeavour;</hi> [as though it were a butt;] syn. <foreign lang="ar">هِمَّةٌ</foreign>.
